title="Second Cambridge Catalogue of Radio Sources">2C</a> 56 (Core),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ned_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-ned-1">[1]</a></sup> CGCG 535-17, MCG +07-02-016, IRAS 00400+4059, 2MASX J00424433+4116074, GC 116, h 50, Bode 3, Flamsteed 58, Hevelius 32, Ha 3.3, IRC +40013</td></tr><tr><td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #6C0;">See also: <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">Galaxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_galaxies" title="List of galaxies">List of galaxies</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Andromeda Galaxy</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/&#594;/: \'o\' in \'body\'">&#594;</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="/&#618;/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">&#618;</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span>), also known as <b>Messier 31</b>, <b>M31</b>, or <b>NGC 224</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Spiral_galaxy" title="Spiral galaxy">spiral galaxy</a> approximately 780 <a href="/wiki/Parsec#Parsecs_and_kiloparsecs" title="Parsec">kiloparsecs</a> (2.5 million <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a>) from Earth, and the nearest major galaxy to the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribas2005_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ribas2005-4">[4]</a></sup> Its name stems from the area of the Earth\'s sky in which it appears, the <a href="/wiki/Andromeda_(constellation)" title="Andromeda (constellation)">constellation of Andromeda</a>.\n</p><p>The 2006 observations by the <a href="/wiki/Spitzer_Space_Telescope" title="Spitzer Space Telescope">Spitzer Space Telescope</a> revealed that the Andromeda Galaxy contains approximately one trillion stars,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jorge_Pe&#241;arrubia2014_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jorge_Pe&#241;arrubia2014-12">[10]</a></sup> more than twice the number of the Milky Way\'s estimated 200 to 400 billion stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frommert_&amp;_Kronberg_2005_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frommert_&amp;_Kronberg_2005-15">[13]</a></sup> The Andromeda Galaxy\'s mass is estimated to be around 1.76 times that of the Milky Way Galaxy (~0.8-1.5<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">12</span></sup> solar masses <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kafle2018_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kafle2018-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jorge_Pe&#241;arrubia2014_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jorge_Pe&#241;arrubia2014-12">[10]</a></sup> vs the Milky Way\'s 8.5<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">11</span></sup> solar masses), though a 2018 study found that the Andromeda Galaxy\'s mass is roughly the same as the Milky Way\'s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kafle2018_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kafle2018-11">[9]</a></sup> The Andromeda Galaxy, spanning approximately 220,000 light-years, is the largest galaxy in the <a href="/wiki/Local_Group" title="Local Group">Local Group</a>, which is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Triangulum_Galaxy" title="Triangulum Galaxy">Triangulum Galaxy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Local_Group#Component_galaxies" title="Local Group">other minor galaxies</a>.\n</p><p>The Milky Way and Andromeda galaxies are <a href="/wiki/Andromeda%E2%80%93Milky_Way_collision" title="Andromeda&#8211;Milky Way collision">expected to collide</a> in ~4.5 billion years, merging to form a giant <a href="/wiki/Elliptical_galaxy" title="Elliptical galaxy">elliptical galaxy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milky-way-collide_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-milky-way-collide-16">[14]</a></sup> or a large <a href="/wiki/Disc_galaxy" title="Disc galaxy">disc galaxy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ueda2014_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ueda2014-17">[15]</a></sup>\nWith an <a href="/wiki/Apparent_magnitude" title="Apparent magnitude">apparent magnitude</a> of 3.4, the Andromeda Galaxy is among the brightest of the <a href="/wiki/Messier_object" title="Messier object">Messier objects</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frommert_&amp;_Kronberg_2007_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frommert_&amp;_Kronberg_2007-18">[16]</a></sup> making it visible to the <a href="/wiki/Naked_eye" title="Naked eye">naked eye</a> from Earth on moonless nights,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> even when viewed from areas with moderate <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Observation_history"><span history</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Distance_estimate"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Distance estimate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Mass_and_luminosity_estimates"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Mass and luminosity estimates</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-7"><a href="#Mass"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Mass</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8"><a href="#Luminosity"><span class="tocnumber">2.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Luminosity</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Structure"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Structure</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Nucleus"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Nucleus</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Discrete_sources"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Discrete sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Satellites"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Satellites</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Collision_with_the_Milky_Way"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Collision with the Milky Way</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Amateur_observing"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Amateur observing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Observation_history">Observation history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Observation history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pic_iroberts1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="569" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pic_iroberts1.jpg/220px-Pic_iroberts1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pic_iroberts1.jpg/330px-Pic_iroberts1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pic_iroberts1.jpg/440px-Pic_iroberts1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pic_iroberts1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Great Andromeda Nebula by <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Roberts" title="Isaac Roberts">Isaac Roberts</a>, 1899.</div></div></div>\n<p>Around the year 964, the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" title="Persian Empire">Persian</a> astronomer <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Rahman_al-Sufi" title="Abd al-Rahman al-Sufi">Abd al-Rahman al-Sufi</a> described the Andromeda Galaxy, in his <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Fixed_Stars" title="Book of Fixed Stars">Book of Fixed Stars</a></i> as a "nebulous smear".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Star_chart" title="Star chart">Star charts</a> of that period labeled it as the <i>Little Cloud</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSOG_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-NSOG-21">[19]</a></sup> In 1612, the German astronomer <a href="/wiki/Simon_Marius" title="Simon Marius">Simon Marius</a> gave an early description of the Andromeda Galaxy based on telescopic observations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aati_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aati-22">[20]</a></sup> The German philosopher <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Immanuel Kant</a> in 1755 in his work <i>Universal Natural History and Theory of the Heavens</i> conjectured that the blurry spot was an island universe. In 1764, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Messier" title="Charles Messier">Charles Messier</a> cataloged Andromeda as object M31 and incorrectly credited Marius as the discoverer despite it being visible to the naked eye. In 1785, the astronomer <a href="/wiki/William_Herschel" title="William Herschel">William Herschel</a> noted a faint reddish hue in the core region of Andromeda. He believed Andromeda to be the nearest of all the "great <a href="/wiki/Nebula" title="Nebula">nebulae</a>", and based on the color and magnitude of the nebula, he incorrectly guessed that it is no more than 2,000 times the distance of <a href="/wiki/Sirius" title="Sirius">Sirius</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herschel_1785_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herschel_1785-23">[21]</a></sup> In 1850, <a href="/wiki/William_Parsons,_3rd_Earl_of_Rosse" title="William Parsons, 3rd Earl of Rosse">William Parsons, 3rd Earl of Rosse</a>, saw and made the first drawing of Andromeda\'s <a href="/wiki/Spiral_galaxy#Structure" title="Spiral galaxy">spiral structure</a>.\n</p><p>In 1864, <a href="/wiki/William_Huggins" title="William Huggins">William Huggins</a> noted that the <a href="/wiki/Spectrum" title="Spectrum">spectrum</a> of Andromeda differs from a gaseous nebula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huggins_&amp;_Miller_1864_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Huggins_&amp;_Miller_1864-24">[22]</a></sup> The spectra of Andromeda displays a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/continuum" title="wikt:continuum">continuum</a> of <a href="/wiki/Frequency" title="Frequency">frequencies</a>, superimposed with dark <a href="/wiki/Spectral_line" title="Spectral line">absorption lines</a> that help identify the chemical composition of an object. Andromeda\'s spectrum is very similar to the spectra of individual stars, and from this, it was deduced that Andromeda has a stellar nature. In 1885, a <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernova</a> (known as <a href="/wiki/SN_1885A" title="SN 1885A">S Andromedae</a>) was seen in Andromeda, the first and so far only one observed in that galaxy. At the time Andromeda was considered to be a nearby object, so the cause was thought to be a much less luminous and unrelated event called a <a href="/wiki/Nova" title="Nova">nova</a>, and was named accordingly; "Nova 1885".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Backhouse_1888_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Backhouse_1888-25">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1887, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Roberts" title="Isaac Roberts">Isaac Roberts</a> took the first photographs of Andromeda, which was still commonly thought to be a nebula within our galaxy. Roberts mistook Andromeda and similar spiral nebulae as solar systems being formed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1912, <a href="/wiki/Vesto_Slipher" title="Vesto Slipher">Vesto Slipher</a> used <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">spectroscopy</a> to measure the radial velocity of Andromeda with respect to our <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a>&#8212;the largest velocity yet measured, at 300 kilometres per second (190 miles per second).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slipher_1913_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slipher_1913-26">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Island_universe">Island universe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Island universe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andromeda_constellation_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="320" data-file-width="320" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Andromeda_constellation_map.svg/220px-Andromeda_constellation_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Andromeda_constellation_map.svg/330px-Andromeda_constellation_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Andromeda_constellation_map.svg/440px-Andromeda_constellation_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andromeda_constellation_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the Andromeda Galaxy (M31) in the Andromeda constellation.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1917, <a href="/wiki/Heber_Doust_Curtis" title="Heber Doust Curtis">Heber Curtis</a> observed a <a href="/wiki/Nova" title="Nova">nova</a> within Andromeda. Searching the photographic record, 11 more novae were discovered. Curtis noticed that these novae were, on average, 10 <a href="/wiki/Magnitude_(astronomy)" title="Magnitude (astronomy)">magnitudes</a> fainter than those that occurred elsewhere in the sky. As a result, he was able to come up with a distance estimate of 500,000 light-years (3.2<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>10</sup>&#160;AU). He became a proponent of the so-called "island universes" hypothesis, which held that <a href="/wiki/Spiral_galaxy#Spiral_nebula" title="Spiral galaxy">spiral nebulae</a> were actually independent galaxies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Curtis_1988_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis_1988-27">[25]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8,_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5700" data-file-width="6289" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg/220px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg/330px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B4_VLT_%E2%80%93_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B5_%D0%B3%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8,_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8B%D0%BC_%D0%B3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Andromeda Galaxy above the <a href="/wiki/Very_Large_Telescope" title="Very Large Telescope">Very Large Telescope</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Triangulum_Galaxy" title="Triangulum Galaxy">Triangulum Galaxy</a> is visible on the top.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1920, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Debate_(astronomy)" title="Great Debate (astronomy)">Great Debate</a> between <a href="/wiki/Harlow_Shapley" title="Harlow Shapley">Harlow Shapley</a> and Curtis took place concerning the nature of the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a>, spiral nebulae, and the dimensions of the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">Universe</a>. To support his claim of the Great Andromeda Nebula being, in fact, an external galaxy, Curtis also noted the appearance of dark lanes within Andromeda which resembled the dust clouds in our own galaxy, as well as historical observations of Andromeda Galaxy\'s significant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doppler_shift" title="Doppler shift">Doppler shift</a>. In 1922 <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%C3%96pik" title="Ernst &#214;pik">Ernst &#214;pik</a> presented a method to estimate the distance of Andromeda using the measured velocities of its stars. His result placed the Andromeda Nebula far outside our galaxy at a distance of about 450,000 parsecs (1,500,000 light-years).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-&#214;pik_1922_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-&#214;pik_1922-29">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Edwin Hubble</a> settled the debate in 1925 when he identified extragalactic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cepheid_variable_star" title="Cepheid variable star">Cepheid variable stars</a> for the first time on astronomical photos of Andromeda. These were made using the 2.5-metre (8&#160;ft 2&#160;in) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hooker_telescope" title="Hooker telescope">Hooker telescope</a>, and they enabled the distance of Great Andromeda Nebula to be determined. His measurement demonstrated conclusively that this feature was not a cluster of stars and gas within our own galaxy, but an entirely separate galaxy located a significant distance from the Milky Way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hubble_1929_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hubble_1929-30">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1943, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Baade" title="Walter Baade">Walter Baade</a> was the first person to resolve stars in the central region of the Andromeda Galaxy. Baade identified two distinct populations of stars based on their <a href="/wiki/Metallicity" title="Metallicity">metallicity</a>, naming the young, high-velocity stars in the disk Type I and the older, red stars in the bulge Type II. This nomenclature was subsequently adopted for stars within the Milky Way, and elsewhere. (The existence of two distinct populations had been noted earlier by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Oort" title="Jan Oort">Jan Oort</a>.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baade_1944_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baade_1944-31">[29]</a></sup> Baade also discovered that there were two types of Cepheid variables, which resulted in a doubling of the distance estimate to Andromeda, as well as the remainder of the Universe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gribbin_2001_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gribbin_2001-32">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1950, radio emission from the Andromeda Galaxy was detected by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hanbury_Brown" title="Robert Hanbury Brown">Hanbury Brown</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cyril_Hazard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cyril Hazard (page does not exist)">Cyril Hazard</a> at <a href="/wiki/Jodrell_Bank_Observatory" title="Jodrell Bank Observatory">Jodrell Bank Observatory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_&amp;_Hazard_1950_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_&amp;_Hazard_1950-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_&amp;_Hazard_1951_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_&amp;_Hazard_1951-34">[32]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Radio_astronomy" title="Radio astronomy">radio maps</a> of the galaxy were made in the 1950s by <a href="/wiki/John_E._Baldwin" title="John E. Baldwin">John Baldwin</a> and collaborators at the <a href="/wiki/Cavendish_Astrophysics_Group" title="Cavendish Astrophysics Group">Cambridge Radio Astronomy Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-van_der_Kruit_&amp;_Allen_1976_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-van_der_Kruit_&amp;_Allen_1976-35">[33]</a></sup> The core of the Andromeda Galaxy is called 2C 56 in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Cambridge_Catalogue_of_Radio_Sources" title="Second Cambridge Catalogue of Radio Sources">2C</a> radio astronomy catalog. In 2009, the first planet may have been discovered in the Andromeda Galaxy. This was detected using a technique called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microlensing" title="Microlensing">microlensing</a>, which is caused by the deflection of light by a massive object.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ingrosso_2009_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ingrosso_2009-36">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The estimated distance of the Andromeda Galaxy from our own was doubled in 1953 when it was discovered that there is another, dimmer type of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cepheid" title="Cepheid">Cepheid</a>. In the 1990s, measurements of both standard <a href="/wiki/Red_giant" title="Red giant">red giants</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Red_clump" title="Red clump">red clump</a> stars from the <i><a href="/wiki/Hipparcos" title="Hipparcos">Hipparcos</a></i> satellite measurements were used to calibrate the Cepheid distances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holland_1998_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holland_1998-37">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanek_&amp;_Garnavich_1998_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stanek_&amp;_Garnavich_1998-38">[36]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_and_history">Formation and history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Formation and history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WISE-_Andromeda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6666" data-file-width="6666" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/WISE-_Andromeda.jpg/220px-WISE-_Andromeda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/WISE-_Andromeda.jpg/330px-WISE-_Andromeda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/WISE-_Andromeda.jpg/440px-WISE-_Andromeda.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WISE-_Andromeda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Andromeda Galaxy as seen by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Wide-field_Infrared_Survey_Explorer" title="Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer">Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Andromeda Galaxy was formed roughly 10 billion years ago from the collision and subsequent merger of smaller <a href="/wiki/Protogalaxy" title="Protogalaxy">protogalaxies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davidge_&amp;_McCoonnachie_2012_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davidge_&amp;_McCoonnachie_2012-39">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>This violent collision formed most of the galaxy\'s (metal-rich) <a href="/wiki/Galactic_halo" title="Galactic halo">galactic halo</a> and extended disk. During this epoch, its rate of <a href="/wiki/Star_formation" title="Star formation">star formation</a> would have been <a href="/wiki/Starburst_galaxy" title="Starburst galaxy">very high</a>, to the point of becoming a <a href="/wiki/Luminous_infrared_galaxy" title="Luminous infrared galaxy">luminous infrared galaxy</a> for roughly 100 million years. Andromeda and the <a href="/wiki/Triangulum_Galaxy" title="Triangulum Galaxy">Triangulum Galaxy</a> had a very close passage 2&#8211;4 billion years ago. This event produced high rates of star formation across the Andromeda Galaxy\'s disk&#8212;even some globular clusters&#8212;and disturbed M33\'s outer disk.\n</p><p>Over the past 2 billion years, star formation throughout Andromeda\'s disk is thought to have decreased to the point of near-inactivity. There have been interactions with satellite galaxies like M32, M110, or others that have already been absorbed by Andromeda Galaxy. These interactions have formed structures like <a href="/wiki/List_of_stellar_streams#Andromeda_Galaxy_streams" title="List of stellar streams">Andromeda\'s Giant Stellar Stream</a>. A galactic merger roughly 100 million years ago is believed to be responsible for a counter-rotating disk of gas found in the center of Andromeda as well as the presence there of a relatively young (100 million years old) stellar population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davidge_&amp;_McCoonnachie_2012_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Davidge_&amp;_McCoonnachie_2012-39">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distance_estimate">Distance estimate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Distance estimate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At least four distinct techniques have been used to estimate distances from Earth to the Andromeda Galaxy. In 2003, using the infrared <a href="/wiki/Surface_brightness_fluctuation" title="Surface brightness fluctuation">surface brightness fluctuations</a> (I-SBF) and adjusting for the new period-luminosity value and a metallicity correction of &#8722;0.2 mag dex<sup>&#8722;1</sup> in (O/H), an estimate of 2.57&#160;&#177;&#160;0.06&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Light-year" title="Light-year">light-years</a> (1.625<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>11</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;3.8<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>9</sup> <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">astronomical units</a>) was derived. A 2004 <a href="/wiki/Cepheid_variable" title="Cepheid variable">Cepheid variable</a> method estimated the distance to be 2.51 &#177; 0.13 million light-years (770 &#177; 40 kpc).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karachentsevetal2006_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Karachentsevetal2006-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-karachentsevetal2004_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-karachentsevetal2004-3">[3]</a></sup> In 2005, an eclipsing <a href="/wiki/Binary_star" title="Binary star">binary star</a> was discovered in the Andromeda Galaxy. The binary<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M31VJ_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-M31VJ-40">[c]</a></sup> is two hot blue stars of <a href="/wiki/Stellar_classification" title="Stellar classification">types</a> O and B. By studying the eclipses of the stars, astronomers were able to measure their sizes. Knowing the sizes and temperatures of the stars, they were able to measure their <a href="/wiki/Absolute_magnitude" title="Absolute magnitude">absolute magnitude</a>. When the <a href="/wiki/Apparent_magnitude" title="Apparent magnitude">visual</a> and absolute magnitudes are known, the distance to the star can be measured. The stars lie at a distance of 2.52<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;0.14<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;ly (1.594<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>11</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;8.9<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;AU) and the whole Andromeda Galaxy at about 2.5<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;ly (1.6<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>11</sup>&#160;AU).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribas2005_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ribas2005-4">[4]</a></sup> This new value is in excellent agreement with the previous, independent Cepheid-based distance value. The <a href="/wiki/Tip_of_the_red-giant_branch" title="Tip of the red-giant branch">TRGB</a> method was also used in 2005 giving a distance of 2.56<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;0.08<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;ly (1.619<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>11</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;5.1<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;AU).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McConnachieetal2005_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-McConnachieetal2005-5">[5]</a></sup> Averaged together, these distance estimates give a value of 2.54<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;0.11<span style="margin-left:0.2em">&#215;<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&#160;ly (1.606<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>11</sup>&#160;&#177;&#160;7.0<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>9</sup>&#160;AU).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avg_dist_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-avg_dist-7">[a]</a></sup> And, from this, the diameter of Andromeda at the widest point is estimated to be 220&#160;&#177;&#160;3&#160;kly (67,450&#160;&#177;&#160;920&#160;pc).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (October 2016)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> Applying <a href="/wiki/Trigonometry" title="Trigonometry">trigonometry</a> (<a href="/wiki/Angular_diameter" title="Angular diameter">angular diameter</a>), this is equivalent to an apparent 4.96<a href="/wiki/Degree_(angle)" title="Degree (angle)">&#176;</a> angle in the sky.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_and_luminosity_estimates">Mass and luminosity estimates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mass and luminosity estimates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass">Mass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andromeda_galaxy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6200" data-file-width="6200" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Andromeda_galaxy.jpg/220px-Andromeda_galaxy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Andromeda_galaxy.jpg/330px-Andromeda_galaxy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Andromeda_galaxy.jpg/440px-Andromeda_galaxy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andromeda_galaxy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Andromeda Galaxy pictured in <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> light by <a href="/wiki/GALEX" title="GALEX">GALEX</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space,_to_scale.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space%2C_to_scale.jpg/220px-Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space%2C_to_scale.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space%2C_to_scale.jpg/330px-Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space%2C_to_scale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space%2C_to_scale.jpg/440px-Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space%2C_to_scale.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Milky_Way_and_Andromeda_in_space,_to_scale.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration showing both the size of each galaxy and the distance between the two galaxies, to scale.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1040" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg/220px-Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg/330px-Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg/440px-Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hubble_Finds_Giant_Halo_Around_the_Andromeda_Galaxy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Giant halo around Andromeda Galaxy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Until 2018, mass estimates for the Andromeda Galaxy\'s halo (including <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">dark matter</a>) gave a value of approximately 1.5<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">12</span></sup>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Solar_mass" title="Solar mass"><var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub></a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jorge_Pe&#241;arrubia2014_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jorge_Pe&#241;arrubia2014-12">[10]</a></sup> (or 1.5 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000000000000_(number)" title="1000000000000 (number)">trillion</a> <a href="/wiki/Solar_mass" title="Solar mass">solar masses</a>) compared to 8<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">11</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub> for the Milky Way. This contradicted earlier measurements, that seemed to indicate that Andromeda Galaxy and the Milky Way are almost equal in mass. In 2018, the equality of mass was re-established by radio results as approximately 8<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">11</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kafle_et_al._2018_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kafle_et_al._2018-42">[39]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup>\nIn 2006, Andromeda Galaxy\'s <a href="/wiki/Spiral_galaxy#Galactic_spheroid" title="Spiral galaxy">spheroid</a> was determined to have a higher stellar density than that of the Milky Way<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalirai_et_al_2006_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalirai_et_al_2006-46">[43]</a></sup> and its galactic stellar disk was estimated at about twice the diameter of that of the Milky Way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chapman_et_al_2006_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chapman_et_al_2006-13">[11]</a></sup> The total stellar mass of Andromeda Galaxy is estimated to be between 8<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">11</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kafle_et_al._2018_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kafle_et_al._2018-42">[39]</a></sup> and 1.1<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">11</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub>.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barmby_2006_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barmby_2006-47">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barmby2007_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barmby2007-48">[45]</a></sup> (i.e., around twice as massive as that of the Milky Way) and 1.5<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">11</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub>, with around 30% of that mass in the central <a href="/wiki/Bulge_(astronomy)" title="Bulge (astronomy)">bulge</a>, 56% in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disc_(galaxy)" title="Disc (galaxy)">disk</a>, and the remaining 14% in the <a href="/wiki/Spiral_galaxy#Galactic_spheroid" title="Spiral galaxy">halo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tamm2012_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tamm2012-49">[46]</a></sup> The radio results (similar mass to Milky Way galaxy) should be taken as likeliest as of 2018, although clearly this matter is still under active investigation by a number of research groups worldwide.\n</p><p>In addition to stars, Andromeda Galaxy\'s <a href="/wiki/Interstellar_medium" title="Interstellar medium">interstellar medium</a> contains at least around 7.2<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">9</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BraunThilkerWalterbosCorbelli2009_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-BraunThilkerWalterbosCorbelli2009-50">[47]</a></sup> in the form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutral_hydrogen" title="Neutral hydrogen">neutral hydrogen</a>, at least 3.4<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">8</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub> as molecular <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> (within its innermost 10 kiloparsecs), and 5.4<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">7</span></sup>&#160;<var>M</var><sub>&#9737;</sub> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstellar_dust" title="Interstellar dust">dust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andromedandust_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andromedandust-51">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Andromeda Galaxy is surrounded by a massive halo of hot gas that is estimated to contain half the mass of the stars in the galaxy. The nearly invisible halo stretches about a million light-years from its host galaxy, halfway to our Milky Way galaxy. Simulations of galaxies indicate the halo formed at the same time as the Andromeda Galaxy. The halo is enriched in elements heavier than hydrogen and helium, formed from <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernovae</a> and its properties are those expected for a galaxy that lies in the "green valley" of the <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_color%E2%80%93magnitude_diagram" title="Galaxy color&#8211;magnitude diagram">Galaxy color&#8211;magnitude diagram</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Andromeda_Galaxy#Luminosity" title="Andromeda Galaxy">below</a>). Supernovae erupt in Andromeda Galaxy\'s star-filled disk and eject these heavier elements into space. Over Andromeda Galaxy\'s lifetime, nearly half of the heavy elements made by its stars have been ejected far beyond the galaxy\'s 200,000-light-year-diameter stellar disk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Luminosity">Luminosity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Luminosity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Compared to the Milky Way, the Andromeda Galaxy appears to have predominantly older stars with ages &gt;7<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">9</span></sup> years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tamm2012_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tamm2012-49">[46]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The estimated <a href="/wiki/Luminosity" title="Luminosity">luminosity</a> of Andromeda Galaxy, ~2.6<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">10</span></sup>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Solar_luminosity" title="Solar luminosity"><var>L</var><sub>&#9737;</sub></a>, is about 25% higher than that of our own galaxy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vdb_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-vdb-56">[53]</a></sup> However, the galaxy has a high <a href="/wiki/Orbital_inclination" title="Orbital inclination">inclination</a> as seen from Earth and its <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_dust" title="Cosmic dust">interstellar dust</a> absorbs an unknown amount of light, so it is difficult to estimate its actual brightness and other authors have given other values for the luminosity of the Andromeda Galaxy (some authors even propose it is the second-brightest galaxy within a radius of 10 <a href="/wiki/Mega-" title="Mega-">mega-</a><a href="/wiki/Parsec" title="Parsec">parsecs</a> of the Milky Way, after the <a href="/wiki/Sombrero_Galaxy" title="Sombrero Galaxy">Sombrero Galaxy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karachentsev2004_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karachentsev2004-57">[54]</a></sup> with an absolute magnitude of around -22.21<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bright_m31_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-bright_m31-58">[d]</a></sup> or close<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCall2014_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCall2014-59">[55]</a></sup>).\n</p><p>An estimation done with the help of <a href="/wiki/Spitzer_Space_Telescope" title="Spitzer Space Telescope">Spitzer Space Telescope</a> published in 2010 suggests an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_magnitude" title="Absolute magnitude">absolute magnitude</a> (in the blue) of &#8722;20.89 (that with a <a href="/wiki/Color_index" title="Color index">color index</a> of +0.63 translates to an absolute visual magnitude of &#8722;21.52,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blue_mag_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-blue_mag-10">[b]</a></sup> compared to &#8722;20.9 for the Milky Way), and a total luminosity in that <a href="/wiki/Wavelength" title="Wavelength">wavelength</a> of 3.64<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup><span style="white-space:nowrap">10</span></sup>&#160;<var>L</var><sub>&#9737;</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tempel2010_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tempel2010-60">[56]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rate of star formation in the Milky Way is much higher, with Andromeda Galaxy producing only about one solar mass per year compared to 3&#8211;5 solar masses for the Milky Way. The rate of <a href="/wiki/Nova" title="Nova">novae</a> in the Milky Way is also double that of Andromeda Galaxy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liller_&amp;_Mayer_1987_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liller_&amp;_Mayer_1987-61">[57]</a></sup> This suggests that the latter once experienced a great star formation phase, but is now in a relative state of quiescence, whereas the Milky Way is experiencing more active star formation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vdb_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-vdb-56">[53]</a></sup> Should this continue, the luminosity of the Milky Way may eventually overtake that of Andromeda Galaxy.\n</p><p>According to recent studies, the Andromeda Galaxy lies in what in the <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_color%E2%80%93magnitude_diagram" title="Galaxy color&#8211;magnitude diagram">galaxy color&#8211;magnitude diagram</a> is known as the "green valley", a region populated by galaxies like the Milky Way in transition from the "blue cloud" (galaxies actively forming new stars) to the "red sequence" (galaxies that lack star formation). Star formation activity in green valley galaxies is slowing as they run out of star-forming gas in the interstellar medium. In simulated galaxies with similar properties to Andromeda Galaxy, star formation is expected to extinguish within about five billion years from the now, even accounting for the expected, short-term increase in the rate of star formation due to the collision between Andromeda Galaxy and the Milky Way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andromeda_Galaxy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Infraredandromeda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1294" data-file-width="3600" decoding="async" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Infraredandromeda.jpg/220px-Infraredandromeda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Infraredandromeda.jpg/330px-Infraredandromeda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Infraredandromeda.jpg/440px-Infraredandromeda.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Infraredandromeda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Andromeda Galaxy seen in <a href="/wiki/Infrared" title="Infrared">infrared</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Spitzer_Space_Telescope" title="Spitzer Space Telescope">Spitzer Space Telescope</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>\'s four <a href="/wiki/Great_Observatories_program" title="Great Observatories program">Great Space Observatories</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2410" data-file-width="8193" decoding="async" height="65" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg/220px-Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg/330px-Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg/440px-Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andromeda_galaxy_Ssc2005-20a1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Image of the Andromeda Galaxy taken by Spitzer in infrared, 24 <a href="/wiki/Micrometre" title="Micrometre">micrometres</a> (Credit:<a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JPL" title="JPL">JPL</a>&#8211;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caltech" title="Caltech">Caltech</a>/Karl D. Gordon, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona" title="University of Arizona">University of Arizona</a>).</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload=\'&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/A_Swift_Tour_of_M31.ogv/854px--A_Swift_Tour_of_M31.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:854px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="185.92" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="A_Swift_Tour_of_M31.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/bd/A_Swift_Tour_of_M31.ogv/A_Swift_Tour_of_M31.ogv.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm;
